19. Final doctrine
This brain should be judged by whether it becomes:

less likely to certify fragile knowledge,

less likely to push learners into harmful conditions,

more accurate about why learners are struggling,

more effective at choosing the right intervention family,

more reliable at building durable mastery,

better at seeing recurrence and systemic drift,

more honest about uncertainty,

and more stable in production.

Your current engine already contains the early forms of many benchmarkable behaviors: proof contracts, multi-model sequencing, persisted risk/warning logic, dwell-aware adaptation, systemic pattern detection, stop-lists, caching, queue-oriented timing outputs, and planner feedback. 

 

 


The next document should define the full repository and module constitution — the actual folder-by-folder architecture, shared packages, engine boundaries, event bus layout, datastore ownership, and interface map you would use to build this full intelligence system cleanly.


proceed

I’m turning the architecture into build-grade repository structure now: package boundaries, ownership, interfaces, event bus, storage domains, and how to keep the codebase from collapsing into one giant “brain” module.

Thought for 18s
Good. Here is the Full Repository and Module Constitution for the academic coach intelligence system.

This takes everything we defined and turns it into a build-grade codebase shape: bounded modules, ownership lines, shared packages, event bus layout, storage domains, interface rules, and anti-chaos constraints.

The right framing is not “one intelligence engine crate.”
It is a workspace of tightly governed intelligence domains.

That matters because your audited nucleus already proves two things:

the current engine is real Rust, not placeholder logic — 12,068 lines across 6 engines 


the engines already exchange persisted state across boundaries, for example Topic → Coverage, Topic → Timing, Topic → Risk/Adaptation, Risk/Adaptation/Timing → Study Planner

So the full repository must support many engines with disciplined interaction, not one oversized module.

1. Foundational repository laws
Law 1
No “brain” mega-module.

Law 2
Every major domain gets a bounded package with:

owned data contracts

owned orchestration hooks

owned write responsibilities

public read interfaces only where needed

Law 3
Shared substrate lives in a dedicated common layer, not copied into engines.

Law 4
Event choreography is centralized as infrastructure, but event semantics belong to domains.

Law 5
Governance is not mixed into product logic. It has its own packages.

Law 6
Read models are separate from source-of-truth state.

Law 7
Content intelligence is a first-class workspace branch, not a side utility.

This one-owner rule avoids silent state corruption.

6. Cross-domain interface constitution
The repository should enforce three kinds of interfaces.

6.1 Query interfaces
Read-only access to domain-owned state.

Example:

diagnosis can query knowledge

decision can query diagnosis, learner, memory, tensions

execution can query decision, content, governance status

6.2 Command interfaces
Explicit actions that ask a domain to perform work.

Example:

planning asks decision for risk refresh

orchestration asks governance for release gate evaluation

content asks knowledge for alignment resolution

6.3 Event subscriptions
Reactive consumers of domain events.

Example:

planning subscribes to timing/risk/adaptation/topic-state events

memory subscribes to intervention/session/outcome events

tensions subscribes to learner/risk/proof/adaptation events

No domain should write directly into another domain’s tables.

7. Dependency rules
Allowed direction of dependency
substrate/contracts/events
        ↓
knowledge/evidence/content
        ↓
learner/diagnosis/tensions
        ↓
decision/planning
        ↓
execution/governance
        ↓
readmodels/api
Hard bans
execution must not mutate diagnosis state directly

content must not choose strategy

memory must not overwrite fresh learner state

planning must not bypass governance for learner-facing release

api must not compute engine logic inline

readmodels must never become a source of truth

8. Event bus layout
I would split the event bus into bounded topics/streams.

Stream families
evidence stream
response.recorded

hint.used

question.skipped

session.block.completed

state stream
concept.state.updated

topic.state.updated

learner.state.updated

tension.updated

diagnosis stream
hypothesis.reranked

misconception.detected

interference.detected

false_mastery.flagged

ambiguity.raised

probe.created

probe.completed

decision stream
teaching.decision.emitted

timing.decision.emitted

risk.assessed

adaptation.event.emitted

protection.rule.created

planning stream
coverage.snapshot.updated

sequence.plan.created

planner.ranking.updated

retest.queue.updated

delayed_recall.queue.updated

execution stream
session.plan.created

session.released

intervention.created

assessment.created

assignment.created

content stream
source.ingested

source.parsed

artifact.packaged

content.gap.detected

content.request.created

artifact.trust.changed

governance stream
confidence.gate.hit

contradiction.detected

arbitration.resolved

policy.hit

decision.trace.completed

memory stream
intervention.outcome.logged

recurrence.detected

systemic.pattern.detected

learner.profile.rebuilt

forecast.updated

This aligns with the audited cross-engine reality you already have, where timing, risk, and adaptation outputs are materially consumed elsewhere. 


9. Anti-corruption layer
This is essential because the codebase will otherwise drift into mixed semantics.

Create explicit mappers between:

raw source content and canonical knowledge graph

raw session output and normalized evidence

engine-internal structs and repository DTOs

source-of-truth rows and read models

Recommended dedicated packages:

crates/contracts/src/mappers/
crates/storage/src/mappers/
crates/content/src/alignment/
This is where “messy outside world” becomes “clean internal truth.”

17. Build doctrine for the repository
The repository should grow by adding bounded domains, not by increasing interweaving.

Every new feature should answer:

Which crate owns this truth?

Which existing crate may read it?

Which events should it emit?

Which read models should consume it?

Which governance rules apply?

Which benchmark family should cover it?

If those answers are fuzzy, the feature is not ready to enter the repo.

18. Final doctrine
The correct repository for this coach brain is not:

one big engine folder,

a few giant service files,

or a loose microservice explosion.

It is:

a Rust workspace,

with domain crates for each intelligence organ,

shared substrate and contracts,

event-driven orchestration,

clear data ownership,

governance as a first-class package,

read-model separation,

content intelligence as a peer domain,

and benchmark infrastructure built into the repo itself.

That matches the reality already visible in your audited engine: real Rust modules, real persisted cross-engine outputs, real planner integration, real caching, and real adaptation/risk/timing coordination.

The next clean artifact would be the actual folder-by-folder workspace skeleton with crate Cargo.toml responsibilities and the first interface files laid out exactly as code scaffolding.


proceed

This is not MVP structure. It is the full-form repository skeleton from day 1, with bounded crates, owned responsibilities, shared contracts, orchestration layers, and the first interface files. It also fits the shape your audited nucleus is already pointing toward: separate Topic, Coverage, Sequencing, Timing, Risk, and Adaptation modules with persisted cross-engine outputs feeding planning behavior.

use chrono::{DateTime, Utc};
use serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};

#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]
pub struct ScoredValue<T> {
    pub value: T,
    pub confidence: f32,
    pub evidence_strength: f32,
    pub freshness: f32,
    pub scope_type: String,
    pub scope_id: String,
    pub computed_at: DateTime<Utc>,
    pub provenance_refs: Vec<String>,
}
crates/substrate/src/wrappers/decision_value.rs
use serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};

#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]
pub enum DecisionHardness {
    Advisory,
    Preferred,
    Required,
    Blocking,
    Constitutional,
}

#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]
pub struct DecisionValue<T> {
    pub value: T,
    pub hardness: DecisionHardness,
    pub confidence: f32,
    pub rationale_refs: Vec<String>,
    pub blocker_refs: Vec<String>,
    pub challenger_refs: Vec<String>,
}
crates/substrate/src/scoring/confidence.rs
#[derive(Debug, Clone)]
pub struct ConfidenceInputs {
    pub evidence_volume_factor: f32,
    pub evidence_consistency_factor: f32,
    pub evidence_diversity_factor: f32,
    pub freshness_factor: f32,
    pub model_alignment_factor: f32,
}

pub fn compute_confidence(i: &ConfidenceInputs) -> f32 {
    let raw = i.evidence_volume_factor
        * i.evidence_consistency_factor
        * i.evidence_diversity_factor
        * i.freshness_factor
        * i.model_alignment_factor;

    raw.clamp(0.0, 1.0)
}

crates/contracts/src/ids.rs
use serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};
use uuid::Uuid;

macro_rules! typed_id {
    ($name:ident) => {
        #[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Hash, Serialize, Deserialize)]
        pub struct $name(pub String);

        impl $name {
            pub fn new(prefix: &str) -> Self {
                Self(format!("{}_{}", prefix, Uuid::new_v4()))
            }
        }
    };
}

typed_id!(LearnerId);
typed_id!(SubjectId);
typed_id!(TopicId);
typed_id!(ConceptId);
typed_id!(SessionId);
typed_id!(HypothesisId);
typed_id!(InterventionId);
typed_id!(ArtifactId);
typed_id!(TraceId);

crates/evidence/src/services/record_response.rs
use anyhow::Result;
use contracts::evidence::{EvidencePacket, ResponseEventCreate};
use substrate::scoring::confidence::{compute_confidence, ConfidenceInputs};

pub struct RecordResponseService;

impl RecordResponseService {
    pub async fn execute(&self, input: ResponseEventCreate) -> Result<EvidencePacket> {
        let confidence = compute_confidence(&ConfidenceInputs {
            evidence_volume_factor: 0.5,
            evidence_consistency_factor: 0.7,
            evidence_diversity_factor: 0.3,
            freshness_factor: 1.0,
            model_alignment_factor: 0.5,
        });

        Ok(EvidencePacket::from_response(input, confidence))
    }
}

crates/learner/src/engines/state_engine.rs
use contracts::learner::{ConfidenceState, FatigueState, LearnerStateSnapshot};

pub struct LearnerStateEngine;

impl LearnerStateEngine {
    pub fn infer_confidence_state(recent_failures: usize) -> ConfidenceState {
        match recent_failures {
            0 => ConfidenceState::Stable,
            1..=2 => ConfidenceState::Fragile,
            _ => ConfidenceState::Collapsed,
        }
    }

    pub fn infer_fatigue(avg_latency_growth: f32) -> FatigueState {
        if avg_latency_growth > 0.50 {
            FatigueState::High
        } else if avg_latency_growth > 0.20 {
            FatigueState::Medium
        } else {
            FatigueState::Low
        }
    }

    pub fn build_snapshot(
        confidence_state: ConfidenceState,
        fatigue_state: FatigueState,
    ) -> LearnerStateSnapshot {
        LearnerStateSnapshot {
            confidence_state,
            fatigue_state,
            ..Default::default()
        }
    }
}

crates/diagnosis/src/engines/hypothesis_competition.rs
use contracts::diagnosis::{HypothesisFamily, HypothesisSummary};

pub struct HypothesisCompetitionEngine;

impl HypothesisCompetitionEngine {
    pub fn rank(mut candidates: Vec<HypothesisSummary>) -> Vec<HypothesisSummary> {
        candidates.sort_by(|a, b| {
            b.posterior
                .partial_cmp(&a.posterior)
                .unwrap_or(std::cmp::Ordering::Equal)
        });
        candidates
    }

    pub fn seed_default_candidates() -> Vec<HypothesisSummary> {
        vec![
            HypothesisSummary::new(HypothesisFamily::PrerequisiteWeakness),
            HypothesisSummary::new(HypothesisFamily::Misconception),
            HypothesisSummary::new(HypothesisFamily::RetrievalWeakness),
            HypothesisSummary::new(HypothesisFamily::PressurePerformance),
            HypothesisSummary::new(HypothesisFamily::Interference),
        ]
    }
}
crates/diagnosis/src/engines/misconception_detection.rs
use contracts::diagnosis::MisconceptionInstance;

pub struct MisconceptionDetectionEngine;

impl MisconceptionDetectionEngine {
    pub fn detect_from_repeated_error_pattern(
        distractor_repeat_count: usize,
    ) -> Option<MisconceptionInstance> {
        if distractor_repeat_count >= 3 {
            Some(MisconceptionInstance::placeholder("repeated_error_pattern"))
        } else {
            None
        }
    }
}

crates/execution/src/builders/session_composer.rs
use contracts::execution::{SessionBlock, SessionBlockType, SessionPlanDraft};

pub struct SessionComposerEngine;

impl SessionComposerEngine {
    pub fn compose_for_misconception() -> SessionPlanDraft {
        SessionPlanDraft {
            objective: "repair misconception".into(),
            blocks: vec![
                SessionBlock::new(SessionBlockType::ConfidenceWarmup, 4),
                SessionBlock::new(SessionBlockType::MisconceptionCheck, 6),
                SessionBlock::new(SessionBlockType::FocusedReteach, 8),
                SessionBlock::new(SessionBlockType::GuidedSolve, 8),
                SessionBlock::new(SessionBlockType::ExplanationCheck, 5),
                SessionBlock::new(SessionBlockType::MemoryAnchor, 3),
            ],
        }
    }
}

crates/planning/src/coverage/mod.rs
pub struct CoverageEngine;

impl CoverageEngine {
    pub fn classify_gap(proof_progress: f32, recent_accuracy: f32) -> &'static str {
        if recent_accuracy > 0.7 && proof_progress < 0.4 {
            "false_mastery_suspect"
        } else if recent_accuracy < 0.4 {
            "weak_foundation"
        } else {
            "firming_needed"
        }
    }
}
crates/planning/src/sequencing/mod.rs
pub struct SequencingEngine;

impl SequencingEngine {
    pub fn choose_model(
        prerequisite_pressure: f32,
        confidence_fragility: f32,
        exam_pressure: f32,
    ) -> &'static str {
        if prerequisite_pressure > 0.7 {
            "dependency_first"
        } else if confidence_fragility > 0.7 {
            "confidence_first"
        } else if exam_pressure > 0.7 {
            "exam_weight_first"
        } else {
            "mixed_portfolio_blend"
        }
    }
}

crates/tensions/src/families/confidence_tension.rs
pub fn compute_confidence_tension(
    confidence_fragility: f32,
    recent_failure_density: f32,
    challenge_intensity: f32,
    recovery_penalty: f32,
) -> f32 {
    (confidence_fragility * recent_failure_density * challenge_intensity * recovery_penalty)
        .clamp(0.0, 1.0)
}

            topic_id: topic_id.to_string(),
            gap_family: ContentGapFamily::MissingTransferItems,
            urgency: 0.8,

    }

crates/orchestration/src/interaction/mod.rs
use anyhow::Result;
use contracts::evidence::ResponseEventCreate;
use evidence::api::EvidenceCommandApi;
use learner::api::LearnerStateApi;

pub struct InteractionOrchestrator<E, L> {
    pub evidence_api: E,
    pub learner_api: L,
}

impl<E, L> InteractionOrchestrator<E, L>
where
    E: EvidenceCommandApi,
    L: LearnerStateApi,
{
    pub async fn handle_response(&self, input: ResponseEventCreate) -> Result<()> {
        let packet = self.evidence_api.record_response(input).await?;
        let _ = packet;
        Ok(())
    }
}
crates/orchestration/src/session/mod.rs
use anyhow::Result;
use decision::api::DecisionApi;
use execution::api::ExecutionApi;
use governance::api::GovernanceApi;

pub struct SessionOrchestrator<D, X, G> {
    pub decision_api: D,
    pub execution_api: X,
    pub governance_api: G,
}

impl<D, X, G> SessionOrchestrator<D, X, G>
where
    D: DecisionApi,
    X: ExecutionApi,
    G: GovernanceApi,
{
    pub async fn build_and_release(&self) -> Result<()> {
        // 1. gather decision pack
        // 2. choose strategy, timing, risk, protections
        // 3. compose session draft
        // 4. run governance
        // 5. release if approved
        Ok(())
    }
}

[package]
name = "api"

[dependencies]
anyhow.workspace = true

apps/api/src/main.rs
mod deps;
mod http;
mod state;

use axum::{routing::get, Router};

#[tokio::main]
async fn main() -> anyhow::Result<()> {
    let app = Router::new()
        .route("/health", get(http::health::health))
        .route("/learners/:id", get(http::learner::get_learner))
        .route("/sessions/:id", get(http::session::get_session))
        .route("/planner/:learner_id", get(http::planner::get_planner));

    let listener = tokio::net::TcpListener::bind("0.0.0.0:8080").await?;
    axum::serve(listener, app).await?;
    Ok(())
}
apps/api/src/http/health.rs
pub async fn health() -> &'static str {
    "ok"
}

9. First interface files I would create immediately
These are the first files I would actually commit on day 1.

crates/storage/src/repos/*.rs

apps/api/src/main.rs

Those files establish:

shared language

shared ids

shared lifecycles

domain boundaries

orchestration entrypoints

persistence contracts

That is the real start of the codebase.

10. First compile-safe stub strategy
To keep the whole workspace buildable from day 1, I would use this rule:

Every domain crate should have:

api.rs

lib.rs

one engine or service stub

one domain model stub

one repo trait stub

That means the workspace compiles before deep logic arrives.

Example minimal lib.rs pattern:

pub mod api;
pub mod domain;
pub mod repo;
pub mod engines;
Example minimal api.rs pattern:

use anyhow::Result;

pub trait DomainApi: Send + Sync {
    fn healthcheck(&self) -> Result<()>;
}
Then replace healthcheck stubs with real methods domain by domain.

11. Anti-chaos rules for contributors
These should be written into docs/repository_constitution.md.

Rule A
No crate may directly write into another crate’s tables.

Rule B
No new enum shared across domains without landing in contracts.

Rule C
No new threshold hardcoded into engine files if it belongs in config.

Rule D
No read model may be used as authoritative decision input without explicit contract.

Rule E
No engine may publish an uncited hard learner-facing decision without governance hooks.

Rule F
No cross-domain call without either:

query API

command API

or event subscription

That is how you stop the repository from collapsing into hidden coupling.

12. First implementation order inside this scaffold
Since you want full-form from day 1, the repo should still be populated in dependency order.

I would populate crates in this order:

substrate

contracts

events

storage

knowledge

evidence

learner

diagnosis

decision

execution

governance

orchestration

planning

memory

tensions

content

readmodels

evaluation

observability

worker apps

That preserves full architecture while keeping implementation sane.

13. What this scaffold buys you
This repository shape gives you:

full day-1 architectural truth

no fake “temporary brain” bucket

strong type boundaries

event-driven orchestration

independent engine evolution

governance as a real package

content intelligence as a peer, not an afterthought

planner and runtime separation

source-of-truth vs read-model separation

clean room for benchmark infrastructure

And that matches the direction your audited nucleus already proves: modular engines, persisted decisions, planner integration, caching, and cross-engine influence are already real in the current system. 

 


The next best step is to turn this scaffold into the actual initial code bundle for the first 10 crates, starting with the root workspace, substrate, contracts, events, knowledge, evidence, learner, diagnosis, decision, and execution.
